amos purchace take hym ſo grete worſhip wol doo ſuche ladyſhip wherof thou ſhalt euermo ryche thanked hyr tho took leue forth went wiſt lytel ment gyle ſorcerye al ſhe took prophecye nectanabus thorugh oute day cam home lay chambre hym ſelf tooke ouertorneth many book thorugh craft arte mage wex forgeth ymage loketh equacions eke conſtellacions loketh con • unction loketh recepcions ſignes houre aſcendent dr • weth fortune aſſent name quene olimpias thylk ymage wryten myddes fronte aboue thus wyn luſt loue nectanabus werk hath dyght whan came within nyght euery wyght falle ſlepe thought wold tyme kepe whiche hath houre apoynted firſt hath anoyn • eed ſond • herbes figure therupon gan coniure thorugh enchauntement lady whiche innocent wyſt thyng gyle mette ſhe ſlepte thylke whyle fro heuen cam lyght whiche al hir chambre made lyght ſhe loked fro ſey hir thought dragon tho whoos ſcherdes ſhynen ſonne hath ſoft paas begonne al chere may toward hed ſhe lay til cam beddes ſyde ſhe lay ſtylle thyng cryde al thynges fayre curtoys debonayre ſtoode hir faſt forme thaunged ſodenly figure man nome hir hir bedde come ſuche thyng ther loue wroȝt wherof ſo hir thought thorugh lykyng god amos childe anone hir wombe • roos ſhe wonder glad alle nectanabus whiche cauſeth alle metred ſubſtaunce ſeeth tyme nygromance ſtynt thyng ſeide carecte ſhe abreyde oute hir ſlepe leueth wele ſooth enery dele clerke hir told gladder many fold hope ſuche glad metrede whiche ſhalle befalle dede longeth ſore day ſhe hir ſweuen telle may gylour pryuete whiche knewe wel ſhe netheles morow ſoone lefte thynges done hym ſent caas told hym pleynly ſaid wel ſhe wyſt ſhe wordes myght tryſt ſhe fond hir auyſyon ryght condycyon whiche hir told tofore prayd hym hertely therfore hir hold couuenaunt forth remenaunt ſhe may thorugh ordynaunce toward god doo ſuche pleſaunce ſhe wakyng myght hym kepe ſuche wyse ſhe met ſlepe couthe gyle ynough herd ioye lough ſaid madame ſhall doo warne yow therto nyȝt cometh play lyf way ſhall lykynge ordeyne ſo comyng ye ne ſhall hym fayle madame yow conuſaile ye kepe ſo pryue wyght el thre haue knowlechyng el myght fare amys ye dyd ought ſhold hym greue thus maketh hir bileue fayneth vnder gyle feyth netheles ſeyth troweth ayene nyght hath within hir chambre dyght gyloure faſt vpon god ſhal pryuely awayte ye make hir wene thus noble gentyl quene ſhe mooſt truſt deceyued nyȝt cam chambre weyued nectanabus hath take place ſawe tyme ſpace thorugh deceyte magyke put hym oute man lyke dragon took forme whiche wold al conforme ſhe ſawe ſweuen thus chambre comen quene lay bed ſyghe hopeth euer cam nyghe god luby ſhe leſſe fere wold hir aſſure yet efte chaunged figure wether lykeneſſe took fygure nobleſſe large horne none fyne gold precious ſtones corowne hede bare ſodenlyche ſhe ware whiche gyle forme turneth man cam bed ſhe lay ſtylle ſhe ſuffred wylle ſhe whiche wende myſdo netheles hapned ſoo al though ſhe parte deceyued yet ſhe hath conceyued worthyeſt al kythe whiche euer fore ſithe conqueſt chyualrye thorugh gyle ſorcerye noble knyght begōne whiche al world hath wōne thus felle thyng falle ſhold nectanabus hath wold gyle hath loue ſpedde gyle cam bedde gyle goth hym oute ageyne ſhrewed chambyrlayne begyle worthy quene hym ſene netheles thyng fals god ſoone goo deceyte helde hym cloos tyl morow cam aroos tho tyme leyſer tho quene told hym al ca ſhe gyle none ſuppoſeth two poyntes ſhe hym oppoſeth one yf god nomore wyll come ayene euermore ſhe ſhal ſtonden acord kyng philip hir owne lord cometh home ſeeth hir grone madame ſeyth lete alone god vndertake whan lyketh yow take company ony throwe day fore knowe ſhall yow nyght wylle ſuche myght kepe yow al blame thy comforte yow madame ſhal none cauſe thus took leue forth goth tho began muſe quene myght excuſe toward kyng falle fonnd crafte amonges alle thurgh hath ſefoul daſited magyke ſo enchaunted flewe forth nyȝt vnto kynges tent ryght lay amyddes hooſt ſlepe mooſt ſefoull hym brought another charme whiche wrought home within chambre ſtylle kyng turneth wylle maketh hym dreme ſee dragon pryuete whiche bytwene hym ye quene ouer made hym wene ſweuen god amoo whan quene aroos toke forth rynge wherin ſtone ſet graue therupon ſone whiche whan cam nyght lyon ſwerd ſyght prente tho mette vpon quenes womhe ſette ſeall goth hym forth way ſweuen went waye tho bygon kyng wake ſighed wyues ſake lay within tent hath greete wōder ment haſted hym ryſe anone ſent wyſe among whiche one clerk name amphyone kynges ſweuen herd bytokeneth anſwerd ſaid ſykerly lyf god hath leyn thy wyf gete ſone whiche ſhall wynne world al withynne lyon kyng beeſtes ſhalle world obeye heeſtes ſwerd ſhal wōne ferre ſhyneth ony ſonne kyng doutif dome netheles come ageyne owne londe wyf child grete founde myght hym ſelf ſtere ne made hir heuy chere whiche couthe ſorowe nectanabus vpon morow thorugh deceyte nygromaunce toke dragon ſemblaunce kyng ſat halle came rampyng among hem alle ſuche noyſe ſuche rore agaſt ſo ſore though ſhold deye anone netheles greueth none goth toward deyſe hye quene nyghe ſtynt noyſe wyſe hir profered ſeruyce leyd honde vpon hir barme ſhe goodly chere hir arme aboute neck ayeneward leyde thus quene hym pleyde ſight al men aboute laſt gan loute obeyſaunce vnto hir make wold leue take ſodenly lothely forme egle gan tranſforme flewe ſet hym rayle wherof kyng grete meruayle plumeth hym pyketh doeth hawke hym wel liketh ſelf ſhoke wherof halle quoke terremote ſaiden alle god ſuche rees forth flygh kyng whiche al wonder ſighe cam chambre alone vnto quene made mone foryeuenes hir prayd knewe wel ſaid child god kyng withoute rod chaſtyſed quene excuſed ſhe ben accuſed gretter euydence yet preſence kyng philip mo whan roode feldes tho feſaunte came cye whiche anone hir ſeye fleyng lete egge doune falle brake among hem alle token therof kepe ſawe oute ſhelle crepe lytel ſerpent oute ground whiche rampeth al aboute round ayene wol haue wonne brennyng ſonne myght ſo deyde therupon clerkes ſeide ſerpent oute went enuyroun ſhelle aboute myght torne ageyne ſhall falle certeyne child world ſhal enuyroune aboue bere crowne hym ſhalle befalle yong age ſhall deſire courage world honde turne ageyne londe bore weye home ward ſhalle poyſon deye kyng whiche al ſawe herd fro day forth ſo ferd ielouſye hath foryete whiche hath child beḡete nectanabus pryuete tyme natyuyte vpon conſtellacion wayteth relacion maketh quene ſhe ſhalle • euery houre appoynteth ſo mynute therof lore due tyme bore child forth therupon fell wondres many one terremote vnyuerſell ſonne took coloure ſtele left lyght wyndes blewe many ſtrengthes ouerthrewe ſee propre kynde chaunged al world forme chaūged thonder fyry beuen cruel vpon heuen euery erthely creature tho thought lyf auenture tempeſt laſt ſeceth child kepte age encreceth alyſaunder name hote whome calyſtre aryſtote techen hym philoſophye endenden aſtronomye thynges whiche couthe alſo teche hym youthe nectanabus took vpon honde euery man may vnderſtonde ſorcerye wende wylle hym ſelf proue ende namely begyle lady whiche withoute gyle suppoſeth ſhe hereth often euyll ſtereth ſhip dreynte therin mydde caas ryght ſo betydde nectauabus vpon nyght fayre ſterre bryght yong lord lad vpon hyghe aboue towre ſyghe ſterres ſuche acounteth ſeeth eche hem amounteth though knewe al thynge yet hath knowlechyng ſhall vnto hym ſelf befalle hath told wordes alle yong lord hym oppoſeth aſketh yf ſuppoſeth deth ſhall hym ſelf deye ſeith fortune aweye euery ſterre hath loſt wonne el myn owne ſonne ſhall ſlayn may fle thought alyſandre pryuyte herof old dotard lyeth ought aſpyeth al ſodenlyche old bone ſhoof ouer wal none ſeyth hym lye doune part wherof ſerueth al thyn art thou knoweſt al mennes chaūce thy ſelf haſt ygnoraunce thou haſt ſaid amonges alle thy perſone befalle neccanabus whiche hath deth yet whyles hym laſteth lyf brethe alyſander ſpak ſeyd w • th wrōg blame hym leid fro poynt poynt al che ca told hie ſonne tho whiche ſory ynough oute dyche fader drough told moder ferde counceyl ſhe herd knew tokenes whiche told nyſt ſhe ſey ſhold ſtoode abaſſhed whyle magyke gyle thought ſhe deceyued ſhe hath man conceyued wend god netheles ſuche degree ſhe myght hir honoure ſaue ſhope body begraue thus nectanabus abought ſorcery whiche wrought though vpon creature thorugh carectis figure mayſtry power creatour nought hym lad ageyne who law crafde vſeth luſt god refuſeth tooke hym deuyls • aft lo profyte hym belaft thyng thurgh wēde haue ſtōde firſt hym exiled londe whiche owne frō kyng made hym vnderlyng ſythen deceyue quene torneth hym mochel •• ne thorugh luſt loue gate hym hate ende couthe abate old ſleyghtes whiche caſt yong aliſander hyn ouercaſt fader whiche hym myſbigat ſlewe grete myſhappe one mys another mys yolde ſo ful oft nectanabus craft myſwent ſo myſfell hym went note helpeth clergy whiche maketh man doo foly namelyche nygromaunce whiche ſtont vpon myſereaunce nota qualiter rex zoraſtes ſtatim cū ab vtero matris ſue naſceretur gaudio magno riſit quo prenoſticum doloris ſubſequentis ſignum figurabatur nam et ipſe deteſtabilis artis magica primus fuit inuentor quem poſtea rex surrie dira morte trucidauit ſic opus operarium conſumpſit ſee euydence zoraſtes experyence arte magyke firſt forth drough▪ anon bore lough whiche token woo ſewyng owne contreuyng found magyke taught forth al hym lytell worth ſurry worthy kyng hym ſlewe endyng yet thurgh hym craft vſed thorugh world accuſed ſhal neuer wel acheue thei ſtont ryght byleue lyche wulle euyl ſponne leſeth hym ſelf hath lytell wonne ende proueth euery thyng saul whiche yt iewes kyng vpon peyne deth forbede arte yet took therof parte phitonyſſe samary yafe hym counceyll ſorcery whiche felle moche ſrowe ſlayn vpon morowe conne moche helpeth moche man yelpeth loke euery ſide magyk may wel betyde thy ſone wol rede thou theſe enſamples drede luſt erthely loue thou ſeche ſo come aboue wherof worldes wonder thou ſhalt euer put vnder good fader graunte mercy euer ſhall beware therby loue ſo euer bifalle suche ſorcery abouen alle fro day forth wyll eſchewe ſo ne wylle purſewe luſt loue ſeche wold yow byſeche •• eſide ſtant loue yow herd ſpeke aboue aſyſandre betaught aryſtotle ſo wel taught kyng belonged wherof herte ſore longeth wyte wold mene reſon wold wene yf herd thynges ſtraunge yet tyme ſhold chaunge peyne leſſe ſomdele good ſone thou ſhalt wele wyſedom euer ſtonde hym vnderſtond doth grete preue ſondry wyſe touchyng ſo hyghe pryſe whiche vnto venus knowe may ſelf knowe whiche courte al forth draw thyng hir lawe netheles knowe wel thou longeth ſore helpeth comune euery thynge comune ſcole philophye yet thynk ſpecyfye bookes comprehended wherof thou myghteſt amended though al connyng vpon forme wrytynge somme parte therof yet hane herde mater hath ferd explicit liber ſextus sequitur liber ſeptimus • mnibus cauſis ſapiens doctrina ſalutē cōſequitur nec habet quis niſi dectus opem naturam ſuperat doctrina viro quod et ortus ingenij docilis non dedit ipſa dabit non ita diſcretus hominū per climata regnat quā magi vt ſapiat indiget ipſe ſcole quia omnis doctrina bona huma regno ſalutem confert hoc ſepti mo libro ad inſtanciam amantis lang uēdi intendit genius illam ex qua philoſophi et aſtrologi philoſophie doctrinā regem allexandrum inbucrunt ſecun • dū aliquid declarare diuidit enim philoſophiam tres partes quarum prima theorica ſecunda rethorica tercia practica nuncupata eſt de quarum condicionibus ſubſequenter per ſingula tractabit incipit liber septimus genius preeſt loue ſone yu haſt praid aboue ſcole ſhal declare ariſtotle eke fare alyſaundre taught ſomdele therof diſtraught matere loue ſytcen ſhryue menu bad nenertheles glad thou ſeeſt thyn apryſe ſuche thynges wyſe wherof thou myght tyme blyſſe ſhall wyſſe wyſedom euery throwe aboue al thyng knowe loues cauſe el thy ſone vnto thyn ere though regyſtre venus yet calyſtre ariſtotle whylome wryte alyſander thou ſhalt wyte lore ben dynerſe thynk fyrſt reherce nature philoſophy whiche ariſtotle clergy wyſe experte ſeyence declared thylke intellygence poyntes pryncipalle wherof firſt ſpecialle theoryk whiche grounded hym whiche al ye world hath foūded whiche comprehended al lore loken ouermore next ſeyence ſecond rethoryk whoos facounde aboue al eloquent telle tale iugement wel man ſpeke laſt ſeyence thre practyke whoos offyce vertu tryeth fro vyce techeth vppon good thewes ſlee company ſhrewes whiche ſtant diſpoſicion mannes fre election practyke enformeth eke rewle worthy kyng ſhal rule realme bothe werre pee lo thys done ariſtotles theſe thre ſcyrncrs hath deuyded nature alſo decydeed wherof eche hem ſhall ſerue firſt whiche conſerue kepar remenaunt whiche mooſt ſuffyſaunt chyef philoſophye therof ſhall ſpecyfye philoſophre told herken kepe thou holde prima creatorem dat ſcire ſciencia ſummi qui capit agnoſcit ſufficit illud ei▪ plura vires quādoqȝ iuuat neſcire ſet illud qd videt ex pediens ſobrius ille ſapit hic tractat de prima parte philoſophie que theorica dicitur cuius natura triplici dotata eſt ſciencia paſſeth ofte right veynes ben bloode man right ſo water floode erthe cours maketh dyuerſe veynes wel ye hylle ye pleynes man may ſee eye hylles mooſt hye may men wel ſtremes fynde preueth wey kynde de melencolica dicendum eſt • e whiche natur • euery kynde myghty god ſo fynde man whiche creature hath ſo deuyded nature none ty • wel acordeth cauſe ſo diſcordeth lyf whiche feleth ſykerneſſe may trouthe degre thus trouthe degre zorobabel mooſt commended wherof queſtion ended receyued hath mede trouthe whiche mannes nede mooſt behouelyche ouer thy trouthe ſpeciall firſt poynt obſeruaunce take vnto gouernaunce alyſander ſeid therupon grounde leyd euery kynges regyment thyng whiche mooſt conuenyent ſet kyng euen world▪and eke heuen abſit auaricia tangat regia corda cuius enim ſpolijs excoriatur humus fama colit largum voluntas per ſecu la regem dona tamen licitis ſuut moderanda modis hic tractat de regi • mageſtatis ſecunda policia▪ quam ariſtotiles largitatē vocat cuius virtute non ſolum propulſata auaricia regis nomen magnificum extollatur ſed et ſui ſubicionum diuiciarum habundancia • cundiores ef ficiuntur next trouthe ſecond polycye found whiche ſerueth worldes fame worſhip kynges name largeſſe whoos pryuelege may auaryce abrege worldes good firſt comune afterward vpon fortune thylk comyn proufite ceſed peple ſtode encreſed lygnage • en grete anone ſinguler beyete ſacrefye vnto mynerue wyte anſwere goddeſſe hir lord ſekeneſſe wherof ſo woo byſene recouer myght hele ayene lo thus ſhe cryed lo thus ſhe prayed tyl laſt voys hir ſayed yf ſhe wold ſake maladye ſuffre take dye hir ſelf ſhal lyue anſwer alceſt hath yeue vnto mynerue grete thonkyng hir deth lyuyng theſe al hole entente thus accorded home ſhe wente chambre whā ſhe came hir buſbond anone ſhe name bothe hir armes hym kyſte ſpake vnto hym hir liſte vpon within thro good wyf ouerthrowe deyed hole haſte may man reſon taſte nexte god aboue trouthe woman loue whome al grace founde myghtyeſt vpon grounde moſt behouely many folde lo thus zorobabel hath tolde tale opynyon fynal concluſyon ſtrengeſt erthely thynges wyne wymmen kynges ſeyth trouthe aboue hem alle myghtyeſt euer falle trouthe ſo ener come may thynge ben ouercome may wel ſuffre throwe laſt ſhal knowe prouerhys trewe ſhal whyle neuer rewe ſo cauſe wende trouthe ſhameles atte ende thynge trouthleſſe may wel ſhameleſſe ſhame hyndereth euery wyght pryuely myght trouthe degree thus trouthe degree zorobabel moſte commended wherof queſtyon ended receyued hath mede trouth whiche mannes nede moſte behouelyche ouer al thy trouthe ſpecyal firſt poynte obſeruaunce take vnto gouernaunce alyſaunder ſayed ther vpon groūde layed euery kynges regymente thynge whiche moſte conuenyente ſette kynge euen bothe world eke heuen abſit auaricia tangat regia corda cuius enim ſpolijs excoriatur humus fama colit largum voluntas per ſecula regem dona tames licitis ſunt moderanda modis hic tractat de regie mageſtatis ſecunda policia quam ariſtotiles largita tem vocat cuius virtute non ſolum propulſata auaricia regie nomen magnificum extollatur ſz et ſui ſubditi om niū dunciarum habundancia iocundi ore efficiuntur nexte trouthe ſecond polecye founde ſerueth worldes fame worſhyp kynges name largeſſe who preuylege may auarice abrege worldes good firſt comune afterward vpon fortune thylke comyn prouffyt ceſed whan peple ſtode encreſed lygnages wexen grete anone ſynguler byȝ •• e drewe euery man partye wherof comyn fyrſt enuye grete debate warees ſtronge laſte emōge men ſo longe tyl man wyſt ne frende ne whiche foo whyl atte laſte euery londe within hem ſelf peple fonde good make kynge whiche myght appeſen al thynge yeue ryght lignages partyng heritage eke al good thus aboue hem al ſtood kyng vpon regalye whiche hath iuſtefye worldes good couetyſe ſyt wel al wyſe kyng betwene leſſe ſette herte vpon largeſſe toward hym ſelf eke alſo toward peple yf ſo ſay yf toward ſelf large free peple take pylle largeſſe weye ſkylle may ſaid auarice kyng grete vyce kyng hehoueth eke flee vpce prodegalyte meſure expence kepe indygence may ſaufe fro nedeth al werke wers ſpedeth nota ſuper hoc qued ariſtotilus ad alexandrium exemplificauit de exactionibus regis chaldeorū ariſtotle vpon caldee enſaumple grete auctorite vnto aliſaunder taughte thylke folke vnſaughte toward hir kyng pyllage wherof hade corage vnto thre poyntes entende wold good dyſpende fyrſt ſhold loke ſtood al owne good yeftes whiche wold yeue myght better leue eke muſt taken hede yf canſe ony nede whiche oughte deffended goodes ben dyſpended mote eke befalle amonge thynges alle se decertes men ben ken eſtate meryte ſhal hem largely acquyte werre peaſe none honoure falle dyſcreaſt whiche myght torne deffame kepe good name holde vnkynde cronycle tale fynde whiche ſpeketh ſom dele matere afterward thou ſhalt hic ſecundum geſta iulij exemplū ponit qualiter rex ſuorum militum quos probos agnouerit indigenciam largitatis ſue beneficijs releuare tenetur ▪ rome purſue right worthy poure knyght whiche came allone ſeyne cauſe courte pleyne iulyus preſence hym lacketh dyſpēce hym none aduocate make plee eſtate though hym lacke plede hym lacketh nought manhede wiſt wel purſe pouer yet thought right receuer penly pouerte aleyed emperour thus ſeyed iulyns lord lawe behelde counceyl withdrawe lacke golde thyn offyce lawe iustyce helpe counceyl vpon trouthe matere iulyus anone aſſygned hym worthy one hym ſelf worde ſpáke knyght wroth fonde lake emperour ſaid thus thou vnkynde iulyus whan thou thy batayle vpon aufrik might reſcue dyd man ſtede thou woteſt woundes fynde ſo bad ne liſt ſpeke one worde thyn owne mowthe thy horde yeue floreyn helpe ſhold yelpe fro forth largeſſe whan ſuche grete vnkyndeneſſe founde ſuche lord thou iulyus knewe wel al ſothe hym tolde wold ben holde vnkynde toke cauſe honde goddes ſonde yaue hym good ynough ſpende euer vnto lyues ende thus ſhold euery worthy kyng take knyghtes knowlechyng whan ſawe nede euery ſeruyce axeth mede whiche haue deſerued thorugh vertu • ape ſerued kyng ſhal deſerue grace though large ſuche place hic ponit exemplum de rege antigo qualiter dona regia ſecundum mame et minus equa diſcrecione moderanda ſunt sitteth wel euery kyng haue diſcreſſyon whan men hym craue may gyfte wyte wherof fynde tale wryte ciuichus power knyght ſomme whiche ouer myght prayed kyng antygonus kyng anſwerd hym thus ſaid ſuche yefte paſſeth power eſtate laſſeth axeth lytel peny yf kyng wold yeue hym ony kyng anſwerd ſmalle hym lord ryalle yeue man ſo lytel thynge vnworſhyp kyng enſaumple kyng may lere yeue manere yf kyng treſour laſſeth without honoure thankeleſſe paſſeth whan hym ſelf wyl ſo begyle note ſhal compleyne whyle ne right hym ſhal releue netheleſſe beleue nota hic qd regis ſtatus ſuis fidelibȝ omni fauore ſupportandus eſt whiche owne londe behoueth euery mannes honde ſette vpon neceſſyte eke kynges ryalte mote euery lyege man comforte good body ſupporte whan ſee cauſe reſonable entendable holde vp right kynges name hym ought blame nota hic ſecundum ariſtotelem qua liter principum prodigalitas pauperta tem induat co • nne •• polecye euer ſpeke matere phyloſophre tolde kyng rule holde modefye adreſſe yeftes vpon ſuche largeſſe seneca ſit alijs benefacito vt tibi non •• g meſure excede yf kyng ſhal nede cauſeth ofte ſendry thynges ben vngoodly kynges man wyl hym ſelf meſure men ſecth ful ofte meſure hym hath forſake ſo doth vſeth prodygalite moder pouerte wherof londes ben deſerte namely whan ylke vyce aboue kynge ſtante offyce hath holde partye cenetous flaterye many worthy kyng deceyueth fallace perceyueth hem ſeruen gloſe pleſe gloſe ben men tellen norice vnto foſteryng vyce wherof ful ofte netheles kyng blamed gyltles nota qualiter principum curijs adula tore triplice grauitate offendunt philoſophre thou ſhalt spake kyng matere ſaid hym wel flaterours coulpable thre errours one toward goddes hye wroth ſyghe myſchyef whiche befalle ſhold fals flaterour tolde toward kyng another whan ſleyght falla feyned wordes make hym wene blacke whyt blew grene touchyng condicion whan doeth extorcion many another vyce moo men ſhul fynde one tho grutche ſpeke ageyn holden vp oyle ſayn al wel euer doth thus fals maken ſoth kynges eye blente wote world went third errour harme comune peple mote comune wronges bryngen ynne aud thus werchen treble ſynne ben flaterours aboute kynge myght werſe thynge aboute kynges regalye vyce flaterye netheleſſe hath ben vſed neuer yet refuſed ſpeke courte ryalle moſt ſpecialle many longe bore whan vyce hem bore ſhold vertuous forth brynge trouth torned leſynge ſayth ageynſt kynde wherof olde enſaumple fynde hic contra vanitates adulandum loquitur et narrat quod cum ariſippus de cartagine philoſophus ſcole ſtudium relinquens ſui principio obſequio magnis adulacionibus pre ceteris carior aſiſtebat accidit vp ipſe quodam die dioginem philoſophum uuper ſocium ſuum virum tam moribus quam probatiſſimum herbas ad olera ſua collectas lauantem ex caſu ad ripam inuenerat cui ait diogene scito ſicut et ego principi tuo placere ſcires huiuſmodi herbas aut celligere aut non lauare indigeres ariſippe certe ſi tu olera tua lauare ſcires blan • icijs et adulacioni • u principi tuo ſeruire non oporteret • mouge theſe olde tale wyſe phyloſophres wyſe trde whilom two ſoole lere vnto athenis fro cartage frendes whan age hem ſente ſtoden longe tyl ſuche lore haue vnderfonge tyme ſurmounte al men accounte hem two grete fame firſt hem right name drogenes hote founde ryote felowe ariſippus hyght whiche moche coude myght atte laſt ſothe ſayne bothe torned home agayne vnto cartage ſoole lete dyogynes beyete worldes good laſſe ne ſought longe lore toke hym onely dwelle home bookes telle hows nygh ryuere beſyde bridge thou ſhalt dwelled toke reſte thought hym beſte ſtudye philoſophye whiche ſo wold defye worldes pompe euery ſyde ariſippe bookes ſyde hath leyed courte wente many wyle many wente flaterye wordes ſofte caſte hath compaſſe • ofte prynce myght pleſe wyſe gate hym • aſe veyne honour worldes good londes rule vpon hym ſtode kyng hym wonder glad al thynge bad bothe courte eke flaterye brought purpoos worldes werke ageyn ſtate clerke philoſophye lefte rich hym ſelf vp lefte • thus ariſippe wylle dyogenes dwellyd ſtylle home loked boke ſought worldes croke veyn honour ne richeſſe al herdes beſyneſſe ſet vertuous thus within owne hows lyueth ſuffyſaunce hauyng fyl perchaunce dyogynes vpon day monthe māy whan theſe herbes ben holſom walked gader ſom gardyn whiche iolytes thought haue thus aboutes whā hath gadred hym liketh ſet hym doun pyketh wyſſhe herbes flode vpon gardyn ſtode nygh bridge tolde ere happeneth whyle ſitteth came ariſippes ſtrete many hors route grete ſtreyght vnto bridge rode houed abode caſte eye nygh felowe dyogenes ſyghe dyd ſawe alſo wherof ſayd hym tho diogenes god ſpede certes lytel nede ſit wortes pyke thou thy prynce coudeſt lyke degree ariſippe ageyn quod thou coudeſt ſo thy wortes pyke truly lytel nede leſſe thou yt ſo worldly wold compaſſe flaterye ſerue wherof thou thynkeſt dyſſerue thy prynces thanke purchace thou myght ſtonde grace getyng lytel good thou wold take thy mood reſon thou myght reſon deme ſo thy prynce queme reſon accordaunt gretely diſcordaunte vnto ſooles athene • thus anſwerd diogene ageyn clerkes flaterye men ſeen aſſemplarye ariſippe wel receyued thylke dyogene weyued offyce courte golde coffre men ſayn philoſophre whiche hath worſhyp halle flaterye paſſeth alle chaūbre courte • uaūceth vpon thylke lotte chaunceth byloued daye note yf ye nay dante poete anſwerde flaterour tale herde vpon ſtryf betwene two ſayd hym ther ben many mo thy ſeruauntes myn poete couyne hath none wyl hym clothe fede flatour may rule lede kyng al londe aboute ſtante wyſe man doute hem folye drawe ſuche comyn lawe comune boece telleth flaterye dwelleth ony londe vnder ſonne ful many thynge begonne whiche better lefte hath ſhewed efte yf prynce wold hym rule romayns rule thylke tyme vſed vyce ſhold refuſed wherof poyntes ben aſſoted playn trouth noted may prynce wel conceyue hym ſelf deceyue hereth wordes pleyne hym nought reſon pleyne warned hym woo fully pre • yd tho whan rome worldes chyef • ſooth ſayer tho leef wold trouthe ſpare worde playn • bare themperour ſothes tolde cronyke yet withholde afterward thou ſhalt accordyng vnto matere hic narrāt ſuper eodem qualiter nuper romanorum imperator cum ipſo triumphator hoſtes bello rome rediret tres ſibi laudes ſignum ſui triumphi precipue debebantur primo quatuor equi abbiſſimi currum quo ſedebat veherent secundo tunica iouis pro tunc indueretur tercio ſui captiui prope currum ad viriuſque latus cathena ti deambularent set ne tanti honoris adulacio eius animum ſuperbiam extolleret quidam ſcurra linguoſus iuxta ipſum curru ſedebat qui quaſi contumatis vocibus improperando notheos hoc eſt noſcete ipſum quia hodie fortunata ſibi proſpera ſunt cras forte verſa rota mutabilis aduerſabitur ſee olde enſaumplerye whilom flaterye toward prynces wel fynde wherof ſo cometh mynde ſone tale vnto thyn ere worthy prince rome thynke tellen whan chaunces ſo byfellen ony emperour tho victorye vpon foo ſo came forth rome ageyn treble honour certeyne wherof magnefyed firſt ſpecefyed whan came ylke tyde chare whiche ſhold ryde four whyt ſtedes ſhold drawe iubyter thilke lawe cote ſhold alſo priſoners eke ſhold goo endlonge chare eyther honde al nobleſſe londe fore • hym come rydyng broughte hym rome token chyualrye none flaterye ſhe wed forth al ſatte chare ryalle beſyde hym rybaud ſet worde ſo beſet themperour al glorye ſaid take thy memorye al pompe al pride lete iuſtice goo ſyde knowe thy ſelf ſo befalle men ſeen oftymes falle thynges men wende ſiker ſtōde though thou victorye haue honde fortune may ſtonde alwey whiche perchaunce another day may turne thou myght ouer throwe ther laſteth thynge throwe theſe wordes moo ribaulde ſat hym themperour hys tale tolde euermore wolde euyl good playnly trouth ſtood ſpareth ſpeketh oute ſo myght euery man aboute day ſolempnyte tale telle wel themperour al openly al cauſe ſtode nobleſſe ſhold vanyte repreſſe ſuche wordes herde lo thylke tyme ferde toward ſo hygh worthy lorde fynde eke recorde whiche cronycle hath auctorized emperour intronyzed hic eciam contra adulacionem narrat qd primo die quo nuper imperator introniſatus extitit latonij ſui ab ipſo conſtanter peterent de quali lapide ſue ſepulture tumulum fabricarent vt ſic futuram mortem commemorans vani tate huius ſeculi tranſitonas facilius reprimeret firſt day corone ryal trone helde feſte paleys sittyng vpon hye deys al luſt may gete whan gladdeſt mete euery mynſtral played euery geſtour ſayed moſte pleſaunt ere atte laſte came maſons ſhullen craue wold bygraue ſtone ſepulture ſholden make ſcripture wold ordeyne vpon tho flatrrye none worthy prynce beiape kyng otherwyſo ſhape good counceyl wyſe hem ſelf wyſe vnderſtoden wel knewen whan ſuche ſofte wyndes hlewen flaterxe ere ſetten nought hertes whan herde wordes feyned pleyne trouthe hath diſdeyned hem ſo dyſcrete toke flaterer beyete hym prynce tho proue ſo tale fynde dede cronycle rome rede hic inter alia geſta ceſaris narrat vnum exemplū precipue contra illos qui cum aſpectu principis alijs ſapi enciores apperere vellent quando que tamen ſimilitate ſapiencie talia comittunt per que ceteris ſtulciores fine comprobantur ceſar vpon ryal trone ſatte perſone hyeſt al pryſe man whiche wold make hym wyſe fyldoun knelyng preſence dyd hym ſuche reuerence though hygh god men grete meruayle worſhyp dede man aroos fro thylke ſtede forth withal ſame tyde goeth hym vp ſyde ſet hym doun pere ſaid yf thou ſitteſt arte god whiche al thynges myght haue doo worſhyp right god otherwyſe yf thou thylke aſſyſe bnt arte man ſuche may ſyt faſte bothe one kynde ceſar anſwerd ſaid blynde thou arte fole wel ſene vpon thy ſelf yf thou wene god thou doeſt mys ſit thou ſeeſt god man alſo thou haſt grete foly whan thou ſuche one ſhal deye worſhyp thy god alweye haſt yeuen ſo vnworthely thus may preue redely thou arte wyſe herde wyſely kyng anſwerde hem newe lore wherof dreden hym brought thynge ere bnt yf treuth reſon ben many ſuche wyſe faynen wordes wyſe al veray flaterye hym whiche wel aſpyr nota qualiter iſta circa principem adultores potius curia expelli quam ad regie mageſtatis munera acceptan policia ſuadente delerent kynde flatour loue brynge hym ſelf aboue euer mayſter fare hym ſelf ſtonde care retcheth nought thus ofte deceyueth wordes ſofte kynges ben innocent thaſtement wyſe phyloſophre ſeyed kyng ſo treſour leyed vpon ſuche folke hath leſſe yet doeth largeſſe • nt harmeth owne honde hym ſelf eke owne londe many ſondry weye wherof yf man ſhal ſeye ſpeke generalle ſuche thynge falleth ouer al ony kyng hym ſelf myſrule phyloſophre vpon rule ſpeaal cauſe ſette whiche euer hath bette gouernaunce aboute kyng vpon 〈◊〉 myſelyef thyng ſeyth ſla •• ye wherof fore partye vyce haue declared hath wytte bywared vpon flaterer beleue whan weneth beſt acheue god worde moſte fro preuen ſo exaumples ther ben many one whiche yf thou wylt knowe one behouely whylom fyl matere hic loquitur vlterius de conſilio aduſantum quorum fabulis principe aures organiȝate veritatis auditum ca • ere nequeunt et narrat exemplū de rege achab oui pro eo qd ipſe prophe • fidelis michee recu auit blandiaas oue adulantis ȝedechye adheſit rex sir • e benedab campo bellator ipſum diuino iudicio deuictum interfecit • monge kynges byble fynde tale credyble one whylom achab hyght whiche al iſrael ryght coude gloſe ſofte • latre ſette lofte arete eſtate made hem ryche wroten wordes lyche trouthe wold forbere hem none eſtate •• contre ſuche toke none tyl atte laſte vpon nede benadab kyng ſurry iſrael grete partye ramoth coloath hote hath ſeced • yote toke counceyl ſondry wyſe hem wyſe netheleſſe vpon caas ſtrengthe hym ioſaphas whiche thenne kyng iudee ſende come whiche thorugh frendſhyp alliaūce nexte hym acqueyntaunce ioram ſone ioſaphath achabbes doughter wedded hath whiche hyght fayr goodelye thus came ſamerye kyng ioſaphath founde kyng achab whan gyder ſpekyng thynge ioſaphath ſaith kynge wold gladly somme trewe prophete matere counceyl myght yeue poynte ſhal dreue tyme ſo befelle ſuche one iſrael whiche ſette hym al flaterye cleped ſedechye hym achab hath ſente cōmaundement hym came ſleyghte hath vpon heed heyght two large horne ſette bra flaterour goeth rampyn • lyon caſt horne vp doun bad men ben good eſpeyre horne perſen eyre ſaith withouten reſiſtence wiſt wel ſcience benadab diſcomfyte whan ſedechye vpon plyte hath tolde tale vnto lord anone one accorde prophetes falſe many • bere vp oyle altho affermed whiche hath tolde wherof kyng achab bolde yaue hem yeftes al aboute ioſaphath grete doubte helde fantaſme al herde prayeng achab ſo ferde yf ony man whiche prophecye hym ſpeke théy gone quod achab one brothel mycheas hyght ne cometh ſyght hath longe pryſon leyen hym lyked neuer yet ſayen goodely word pleſaunce netheleſſe thyn inſtaūce ſhal come may say hath ſaid many day yet ſaid neuer wele tho ioſaphath gan ſomme dele gladen hym hope trouthe bade hym withouten ſlouthe men hym ſhold f • tte anone fro hym gone whan came tolden vnto mycheas manere ſedechye declared hath prophecye therupon praye hym fayre wyl ſay contrayre wherof kyng may dyſpleſe • ſo ſhal euery man eſed may helpe hym ſelf alſo mycheas vpon trouthe tho herte ſette hem ſeyth al belongeth vnto feyth none feyned thynge wyl telle vnto kynge ferre god hath yeue hym grace thus came prophete ye place kynges wylle herde therto anone anſwerde vnto hym wyſe lyege lord whiche ſhe ladde chyef counceyl hadde hem lefte ony brethe made hem blede dethe veſſel ſtode whan fulfilled blode caſte tyraunte therin ſaid thus myght thou wynne luſtres thyn appetyte blode whylom within chambre vpon nyght ſteuard hows knyght forthwith chamberleyn alſo counceyl bothe two ſtoden chymne gyder ſpekyng al thre happeth kynges fole sat fyre vpon ſtole bable played yet herde al ſayed therfore toke hede kyng hem axeth rede ſuche matere came mowthe hym tolde couthe whan al ſpoke ment kyng al hole entente thenne atte laſte hem axeth kyng men tellen emong folke touchyng name pris blame right herde ſayn bad hem telle playne peynte ſoth forbere thylke feyth hym bere ſtuard firſt vpon thynge gafe anſwer vnto kynge thought gloſe matere ſaid ferre name good honourable thus ſteward fauourable trouth p • yne ne tolde kyng axeth ſholde chamberleyn auyſe ſubtyl wyſe ſomdele thouȝt vpon feythe hym tolde al peple ſeyth yf counceyl trewe wyſt wel knewe hym ſelf ſhold worthy kyng degree thus counceyl accuſeth partye kyng excuſeth fole herde al caas tyme goddes wylle se • th ſayden ynough hem ſcorne bothe lough kyng ſayd tho syr kyng yf ſo wyſdom thyn owne mode thou thy ſelf good thy counceyl ſhold bad kyng therof merueyle whan fole ſo wyſely ſpacke hym ſelf fonde lacke within owne conſcience thus felith euydence goddes grace • nſpyred maketh yt good counceyl deſired put awey vycious toke hym vertuous wrongful lawes ben amended londes good wel dyſpended peple nomore opreſſed thus ſtood euery thyng redreſſed kyng propre wyſe hath ſuche hym ſelf counceyl may fayle euery counceyl ſought firſt wyſe knyghtes olde tale tolde counceyllen hym manere loue glad chere foryeue graunte al axed fader taxed ſo may reygne acheue thyng ſhal hym litel greue kyng hem herde ouer paſſeth wit cōpaſſeth yonge thynge wyſe theſe olde men deſpyſ • ſaiden ſit ſhal ſhame euer vnto thy worthy name thou ne kepe thy right thou arte thy yonge myght thyn olde fader gate ſay vnto peple plate whyle thou lyueſt thy londe leſte fynger thyn honde ſhal ſtrenger ouer al thy fader body alle thus alſo ſhal thy tale hem ſmote roddes ſmale ſcorpyons thou ſhalt hem ſmyte thy fader toke lite thou thynkeſt take mychel thus ſhalt thou make hem drede ſore grete herte thy corage holde hem ſeruage yong kyng hym hath cōformed done laſte enformed hym vndoyng whan came ſpekyng hath yonge yonge cauſe wente counceyl good reygne fro rightful blood euer afterward deuyded may prouen caas yonge coūceyl warme men ware dothe ofte harme olde age counceyl ſerueth luſty yongth thonke deſerueth perchaunce ſo gardyn tho meſſager forth kyng whan tolde thyng maner ſtode turquynus vnderſtode meſſage ferde anone toke honde yerde gardyn gone lyly croppes one one ſprongen oute ſmote ſtode aboute ſaid vnto meſſengere lo thynge shal ſtede thyn anſwere wyſe bere thou ſhall vnto ſone telle lenger wold dwelle toke leue goeth alle vnto lorde tolde hym alle fader whan arrous herde hym telle ſo anone wyſt mente therto ſet al entente tyl thorugh fraude trechery • prynces h • edes gabye hath ſmyten al wonne fader came • fore ſonne towne romeyns toke ſlewe cyteſeyns without reſon pyce ſpareth degre ſpede conqueſte lete make ryche feſte ſolempne ſacrefyſe phebus temple wyſe whan romayns aſſembled preſence hem al vpon auter al dygkt fyres lyght vnder auter ſodeynly hydous ſerpent openlye came hath deuoured • alle ſacrefyſe eke alle fyres queynte forth anone came ſo gone depe grounde ageyn euery man began ſ • yn lord may ſygnefye therupon praye crye phebus myȝt knowe cauſe ſame throwe gaſtely voys al herde romayns wyſe anſwerde ſaid wickedneſſe pride vnrightwyſneſſe tarquyne ſone hath ſacrefyſe waſted ſo myght ben axceptable vpon ſuche ſynne abhomynable ouer yet hem wyſſeth ſaith hem firſt kyſſeth moder ſhal take wreche vpon wronge ſpeche ben within hertes glade though ſemblaunce made ther knyȝt buitꝰ hyght al haſte myght groūde fyl kyſte none hem cauſe wyſte wende ſporned perchaūce ſo torned brutus al another mente knewe wel entente therthe euery mānes kynde moder blynde ſawe ſo ferre whan leften cyte comen home rome ageyn euery man romeyn moder hath hir bende kyſt eche hem wende firſt vpon chaunce torquyne vengeaunce herden phelus ſeyn euery tyme hath certeyn muſt nedes thenne abyde tyl afterward vpon tyde hic narrat qd cum tarquinus obſidione ciuitatis ardee vt eam deſtru eret intentus fuit arrous filius eius romam ſecreto adiēs domo collatini heſpitatus eſt vbi de nocte illam caſtiſ ſimam dominam ſecrete lucreciam yma ginata fraude vi oppreſſit vnde illa pre dolore mortua ipſe cum tarquino patri ſuo tota clamante rom impꝑm̄ exilium delegati ſunt tarquinus made vnſkylfully werre faſt ageyn towne walles ſtronge ardea cleped longe caſte ſege aboute may man paſſe befyl vpon nyght arrous ſouper dyght parte chyualrye hym ſowpe companye hath bede whan comen ſette ſowper emonge wordes glade arrous grete ſpekyng made tho beſte wyf rome began ſtryf arrous ſaith hath beſte iangle withouten reſte tyl atte laſte one collatyne worthy knyght coſyne arrous ſaid hym wyſe qd none empriſe ſpeke word dede therof take hede anone thy ſame tyde lepe thy hors lete v ryde may knowe bothe two vnwarely wyues ſhal trewe aſſaye arrous ſaith one nay horſbacke anone lepte ſuche manere thynge ſlepte rydyng forth tyl come al pryuelye within rome ſtraūge place doun lyght toke chambre ſyght ben dyſgyſyd throwe lyfe ſhold hem knowe paleys firſt ſouȝt ſee thynge lady wrouȝt arrous made vaunte hir ſawe al glad ſemblaūt al ful myrthes bordes emonge al wordes ſpake hir huſbond whan al vnderſtonde thylke place hem lyſte gone hem forth none wiſt beſyde thylke yate bra collacea cleped collatyn hath dwellyng founden home ſittyng lncrece wyf al enuyronned woman abandoned werche ſhe wrought alſo al bade hem haſte ſayth ſhal huſbondes ſwerde ſpere lyeth ſiege grete dyſeſe yf ſhold hym dyſpleſe wold god hym certes tyl may sōme good tydyng eſtate herte euer vpon debate ſo al men wytneſſe ſuche hardyneſſe he▪can hym ſelf ſpare al moſte care whan walles ſhold aſſayle yf wyſſhes myght auayle wold groundeles pytte ſo ſiege vnknytte huſbond ſye water eye aroos ſhe ne myght ſtoppe men ſeen dewe bedroppe leues floures eke right ſo vpon whyt cheke wooful ſalte teeris felle whan collatyn hath herde hir telle menyng trewe herte none hir ſterte ſaid loo good dere come yon ye moſt bouen ye ſayn ſhe goodely chere ageyn byclypte hym armes ſmale colour erſte pale beaute reſtored myght mored kynges ſone nyghe lady herde ſyghe thynges ben befalle reſon wyttes alle hath loſte loue vpon parte came fyry darte ſuche woūde hym hath ſmyte muſt nedes fele wyte ▪ thylke blynde maladye cure ſurgerye helpe yet nethelees thylke tyme helde pee countenaunce made openlye wordes glade coude manere ſpake made frendely chere tyl tyme goe collatyne hym alſo leue toke ſo nyght al haſte myght ryden ſyege ageyn arous ſo woo byſeyn thouȝtes vpon hym rōne al brode ſonne bedde goeth reſte thenke vpon beſte fayreſt forth alle euer ſawe euer ſhalle hym thought corage portreyed ymage fyrſt fetures hir face nature al grace womanlye bewte byſette myght bette hir yelow treſſed hir atyre ſo wel adreſſed ſhe wepte al thouȝt ſhe ſpake ſhe wrouȝt foryeten hath dele al aketh hym ſo wele worde dede hir lacked nouȝt womanhede thus tyrānyſſhe knyght ſoupled halfe right none hede toke myght ſomme croke al though ageyn hir wylle luſtes fleſſh fulfylle loue reſonable honour remeuable ought wel ben aduyſed hath luſte aſſyſed wyth medlyd loue tyrānye hath founde vpon trecherye weye thynketh holde ſaith fortune vnto bolde fauourable helpe thus within hym ſelf yelpe wylde man vpon treſon began vp ſterte forth wente horſbacke entente knewe wyglt name nexte day tyl came vnto cellocea yate rome yt ſomdele late right euen vpon ſonne ſette ſhape nette hir innocence berrappe ſhold ſo myſhappe pryu • lye euer myght rode hors alyght tofere cellatynes inne al frendeliche goeth hym coſyn houſe ſhe good ſponſe lucrece ſhe hym ſyghe goodely chere drewe hym nyghe ſhe al honour ſuppoſeth hym ſo ſhe dare oppoſeth ſtode hir buſbond tho dyd hir vnderſtonde tale feyned wyſe right wold hym ſelf deuyſe wherof myght hir herte glade ſhe better chere made whan ſhe glad wordes herde hir buſbond ferde thus trouthe deceyued ſhye treſon perayued hir mente al good feſtes ſtode ſouper right wel arayed yet hath worde aſſayed ſpeke loue degre couert ſubtylte frendely ſpeches affayteth tygre tyme awayteth hope catche • raye herdes aweye whan haue ſouped halle ſayth ſlepe hym falle prayeth mote goo bedde al haſte ſpedde hir thought done euery thynge redy ſone brought hym chambre tho ann toke hir liue forth goo hir owne chambre ſhe wende certeynly frende foo wherof fyl mochel woo tyraunt though lye ſofte bedde roos ful ofte goeth aboute leyed ere herken tyl al bedde goon ſleped faſte vpon hym ſelf caſte mantel ſwerde al naked toke honde ſhe vnwaked bedde laye ſhe mette god wote dore vnſhette pryue lye none herde ſofte paas forth ferde vnto bedde ſhe ſlepte al ſodeynlye crepte hir bothe armes toke worthy wyf awoke tenderneſſe womanhede hir voyce hath loſte pure drede one worde ſpeke ſhe ne dare eke bad hir ware yf ſhe made noyſe crye ſayd ſwerde laye faſt bye ſlee hir hir folke aboute thus brought hir doubte lyke lambe whan ceſed wolues mowth ſo ſhe ſeſed lucrece naked fonde wherof ſhe ſwouned honde ſaith laye dede oppreſſed al hym adreſſed luſt toke hym lyſte goeth none wiſt owne chambre ageyn cleped chamberleyn made hym redy ryde thus lecherous pryde hors lepte forth rode ſhe bedde abode whan ſhe wyſt gone cleped lyght anone vp aroos longe day kyſt aweye hir freſſhe araye ſhe hath world forſ •• toke vpon clothes blake euer vpon contynueng right men ſee welle ſprynge eyen ful wooful treas hir hangyng aboute hir eerys wepte man wyſt whye yet emonge ful pytouſlye prayed nolden dretche hir huſbond fetche forthwyth hir fader eke alſo thus comen bothe two brutus came collatyne lucrece coſyne wenten al thre chambre myght ſee woofulleſt vpon molde wepte ſhe water ſholde chambre dore anone ſtoke haue ought vnto ſpoke ſee hir clothes al dyſgyſed ſhe hath hir ſelf deſpyſed hir heer hangyng vnkempt aboute netheleſſe ſhe gan lowte knele vnto hir huſbonde wold fayne haue vnderſtonde cauſe ſhe fared ſoo ſofte wordes axeth tho may good ſwete ſhe thouȝt hir ſelf vnmete leſte worthe wymmen alle wooful chere lete doun falle ſhame coude vnnethes loke therof good hede toke prayden hir al weye ſhe ne ſpare ſaye vnto hir frendes hir ayleth ſhe ſo ſore hir ſelf bewayleth ſothe wold mene ſhe hath hir ſorowe grene hir woo telle thenne aſſayeth tendre ſhame worde delayeth ſondry tymes ſhe mente ſpeke vpon poynte ſhe ſtente hir beden euer one telle forth vpon whan ſhe ſawe ſhe moſte nede hir tale bytwene ſhame drede tolde without peyne wold hir wo • reſtreyne hir huſbond ſory man comforteth hir al ſwore eke hir fader bothe hir wrothe ageynſt hir wylle prayden hir ſtylle hir hane al foryeue ſhe thought leue hem wyl foryeueneſſe ſaid thylke vnkyndeneſſe hir body wrought al ſo ſhe myght nonght afterward world ne ſhalle reprouen hir forth alle ony man therof ware naked knyf ſhe bare within mantel priuelye betwene hir hondes ſodaynlye toke thorugh hir herte thrōge fyl groūde euer amonge whan ſhe fyl ſo ſhe myght hir clothes hir honde ſhe right man dounward fro knes shold ony thynge hir ſee thus laye wyf honeſtlye al though ſhe deyed woofullye tho ſorowe ſeke hir huſbond hir fader eke ſwoune vpon body felle may mannes tonge telle anguyſſhe brutꝰ hem toward hym ſelf herte kepte succeſſe anone lep •• blody ſwerde pulleth ſwere goddes al aboute therof ſhal venge • unce ſhe tho made c • untenaunce h •• b • dely eye atte loſte th •• kyng vp caſte thought anone al herte hath ſette fyre began flo •• e deſyre longeth vnto mayden •• de ſent yf myght ſpede blynde luſtes wylle thynge myght fulfil ſtode vpon maryage knyght ful grete •• gnage ilyaus hyght accordeth hir faders ſyght ſhold douȝter wedde cauſe fully ſpedde hir fader romanye leder chyualrye gouernaunce hath vndertake vpon werre take goeth al ye ſtrengthe men armes mariage lefte ſtode vpon accorde tyl efte kyng herde telle mayde ordeyned mariage thought another thylke tyme broder marcus claudius hote man grete ryote right kyng hym ſelf two gyder vpon caas coūceyl founden weye marcus claudius ſhal ſaye ſhe weye couenaunte ſeruyce apurtenaunte hool none man vpon ſaith euery poynte wytneſſe take sy ſ • e ſ • al forſake whan ſhape ſo lawe tho hir fader abſent ſomned aſſent come preſence kynge ſtode anſwer thynge hir frendes wyſten al wele falſehede euery dele comen kyng ſayden • pon comune lawe prayden noble worthy knyght hir fader comune right thylk tyme falle lay profit alle vpon wilde feldes armed ſhold harmed ne ſhamed oute thus preyden al aboute al clamour herde kyng vpon luſte anſwerde yaue hem onely dayes two reſpyte wente tho ſo ſ • orte tyme appere hir fader myght manere • therof deceyued lyuyus al conceyued purpoos kynge tofore thought therfore al haſte came rydyng lefte vpon felde lyggyng ooſte tyl came ageyn thus worthy capteyn appered redy daye al euer reſon maye lawe audyence doth doughter vpon ſoth marcus hir accuſed hath tofore courte excuſed kyng ſaw purpoſe faile • ſleyght myȝt auayle combred luſtes blynde lawe torned kynde half wrath though preſence hem al deceyued concupiſcence yaue broder ſentence bad hym ſhold ceſe doughter make hym wel eſe al within owne entent wyſt cauſe went broder hath wyte hym ſelf wyte thus mayden wronge whiche vpon kynge alonge ageyn hym none appele fader wyſt wele wherof vpon tyrannye luſte lecherye doughter ſhold dyſceyued illicius weyued vntaily fro mariage right lyon fro rage drede ſette counte note pyte ſhold amounte naked ſ • e • de • ulled oute amonges al route th •• ſte thorugh doughter ſyde al alowde thus cryed lo take hir ye wrongful kynge leuer vpon thynge •• e fader mayde though ſhe • de men ſayde lyf ſhe ſhamed therof euyl named tho bade kyng men ſhold •• ſte body thylke heſte lyke chaced wylde h • houndes whan feleth ſore proueth goeth forth weye ſuche wyſe ſaye worthy knyȝt ſwerd hōde weye made hym wonde none hem ſtrokes kepte thus vpon hors bylepte ſwerd droppyng blode within doughter ſtode came power rome tolde hem al caas ſaid hem myght vpon wronge matere better redreſſe home grete vnright • iſneſſe warre ſtraunge place lefte home hir owne grace thus ſtant • euery mannys lyf • partye wyf doughter yf paſſyng another beute meruayle ſy • apurtenaunte afore hir eye kyng hath hym myſbor • othes haue al sw • • wyl ſtonde ryght thus one acorde vp right rome one home ag •• n torne ſhortely ſayn tyrannye came mowthe euery man ſaith couthe pryuy trecherye set vpon lecherye came openlye mannes ere brought comyn fire euery man perylle dradde hym ſo hem euerladde thy worſe falle thorugh comyn counceyl h • alle haue wronge kyng depoſed hem ſuppoſed counceyl ſtode ledynge lawe vnto • brynge •• yuen penaunce longeth ſuche gouernaunce thus vnchaſte chaſtiſed wherof myght ben aduyſed ſhold afterward gouerne euydence lerne good kyng eſchewe luſte vyce vertu ſewe exemplum • ualiter p • eo quod illi ſeptem viri qui ſat • e raguelis fille magi propter concupiſ tēciam quam propter matrimonium voluptuoſe nupſ •• unt vnus poſt •• um omnes prima nocte demone aſmodeo ſingillatim ingulati interierunt make partye toucheth polecye chaſty • e ſpecialle f •• concluſion fynalle euery luſte eſchewe grete enſaumple may argewe • age towne mede ther mayde rede sarra ſhe hyght raguelle hir fader ſo byfelle body bothe vyſage none ſo fayre lygnage ſeche emonge hem al ſhe wherof ryche cyte luſty folke couden loue aſſot • vpon hir loue axen hir wedde one laſte ſpedde lykyng haue luſte weddyng within herte caſte hym repenteth atte laſte fyl fyrſt nyght whan bedde dyght thynge god • eſecheth al onely luſtes ſecheth bedde fully warme toke hir arme aſmode fende helle ſerueth bookes telle • mpte man ſuche wyſe redy thylke empryſe hath ſet ſuche delyte vengeth ſuche plyte nec • e hath wronge two yonge wyf woo tho wyſt thynge men •• netheleſſe yet thus wente onely fyrſt man th • began syx hir huſbondes aſmode take hondes al bedde deyden whan yt hande toward hir leyde • nought lawe maryage ylke fyryrage • n wyl lawe excede wyl take hede fyl matere ther myght wel ſothe whan ſhe wedded thobye raphael companye taught hym honeſte aſmode wan nought thylke fe • te yet th • wylle h •• luſte ſo goddely ladde • bothe lawe kynde ſerued wherof hath hym ſelf preſerued fyl ſentence another euydence enſaumple man may ſee whan lykyng degre mariage may forſuey wel ought weye luſt better aduyſed god lawe hath aſ • yſed wel reſon kynde beſtes wold bynde onely lawes nature mannes creature god gaue hym reſon forth alle wherof nature ſhalle vpon cauſes modefye ſhal lecherye yet ſhal luſtes haue ben lawes bothe ſaue euery thyng put ſclaūdre whilom kyng al • ſanndre wyſe phyloſophre taughte whan firſt bore caughte onely vpon chaſtyte onely vpon al honeſte wherof kyng hym ſelf may taſte trewe large iuſt chaſt • hym ought reſon forthwyth vertu pyte thorugh whiche thonke deſerue toward god preſerue hym peple al welthe richeſſe henour helthe world elli eke ſone tofore ſpeke ſhrifte ſo thou ſaydeſt thyn eſe thou preydeſt thy louethro • be aſſe wold telle wyſſe forme ariſtotiles lore haue ſayd ſomdele enſaumples aſſaye yf • thy paynes myght laye thorugh ony thynge ſay weye fader praye ye haue tolde thanke thousand folde tale founden myn ere yet herte elly • may ſelf reſtreyne nam euer loues peyne suche lore coude neuer gete myght make foryete • • nte yf ſo ſlepte tydes ay ne kepte thynke loue lalbe • erte withdrawe thy good fader dere •• ue ſpeke matere •• uc • yng loue begonne yf ther ought ouer ronne •• ought foryete lefte behynde falleth vnto loues kynde wherof nedeth ſhryue axeth ſo whyle lyue myght amende amys good dere ſone yi thy ſhryfte make pleyne ie yet nomore ſayne loue vnaduyſed thou ſhalt wel aduyſed vnto thy ſhryfte bylongeth poynte vpon loue hongeth laſte al tho wyl ſlewe ho explicit liber ſeptimus incipit liber octau •• que fauet ad vicium vetus • modo regula coufert nec non econtra qui docet ordo placet ce • u amor dudum non dum ſua lumen cepit quo venus impoſ • tū deuia fallit iter poſt quam ad inſtanciam amantis confeſſi confeſſor genius ſuy hijs que ariſtotiles regem aloxandrum edocint vna cum aliarum cronicarū exemplis ſerioſe tractauit iam vltimo iſto oc cauo voluminead confeſſionem amoris cauſa regrediens tracttare ꝓponit ſuper hoc qd non vlli premordia nature ad • ibitum voluptuoſe conſequentes nullo humane racionis arbitrio ſen eccleſie legum impoſicione ſuis exceſſi bus debite reſrenantur vnde quatenus amorem conceruit amantis conſcienciā pro finali ſui confeſſionis materia genius rimari conatur myȝty god vnbegon stante hym ſelf hath begon al thynges wylle heuen lyſte fulfille al ioye syt entronyſed ſee hath aungels hym ſerue suche hym lyketh preſerue note forueye lucyfer put albeye al route apoſtaſyed ben hym alyed heuen helle aungels fendes felle ny ioye light derke ony nyght paynes ſhal endeleſſe yet paynes netheleſſe plente ben blake wherof ſyght may take thus whan thynges ben falle lucyfers courte falle dedely pryde hem hath conceyued none forthwyth purueyed thorugh hym al cum rege pro filia ſua erudienda retentus eſt appollynus mene tho toke leue kyng quene worthy mayde alſo prayed vnto hir fader tho ſhe myght yonge man tho ſciences lore haue wyſe kyng hir graunteth hir appriſe hym ſelf therto aſſent thus accorded went al euer may yonge fayr freſſhe may coude ſhold enforme ful aſſented forme qualiter filia regis appolinum ornato apparatu veſtiri fecit et ipſe ad puelle doctrinam quam pluriꝰ famulialiter intendebat vnde placata puella amorem appolini exazdeſcens infirmab • tur toke lette nyght whan morow right vnto yonge man tyre clothes good attyre golde ſyluer ſpende worthy yonge lady ſende thus ſhe made hym wel eaſe al pleſe hir ſerueth wel fayr ageyn taughte hir tyl ſhe thas certeyn harpe cytole rote many tewne many note vpon muſyque vpon meſure hir harpe temprure taughte hir wel roel couthe men ſayn frele youthe le •• er contynuaunce mayde fyl vpon chaunce loue hath mad hym quarele ageynſt yongthe freſſh frele mangre wheder ſhe wyl nouȝt mote al hertes thought loue loue obeye ſhe ſhal ful ſore obeye wote euer emonge ſhe feleth towchyug man tyre hir herte hote ony fyre whyle cale ſhe reed ſhe pale right condycyon hir ymagynacyon euer emonge thoughtes alle hir thought may befalle ſhe laughe ſhe wepe wold hir good name kepe fere womannyſſhe ſhame erneſt game ſtante loue ſuche plyte ſhe hath loſte al appetyte mete drynke nyghtes reſte ſhe note beſte thynke al hir fylle holde hir ofte tymes ſtylle within hir chambre goeth oute kyng hir lyf doute wyſt thynge mente fyl tyme wente walke prynces ſones thre came fyl knee qualiter tres filij principum filiam regis ſingillatim vxorem ſuis ſupplicacionibus poſtularent eche hem ſondry w • ſe byſought proferith ſeruyſe myght doughter haue kyng wold hir honour ſaue saith ſhe ſeek ſpeche tho tyme beſeche eche hem make bylle bad wrytc owne wylle name fader good whan ſhe wyſt ſtood hyr lylles ouer ſeyn ſhold haue anſwer ageyn counceyl glad wrote kyng hem bad euery man owne bock kynges honde bytook doughter ſende prayed hir make ende wrote ageyn hir owne honde right ſhe herte fonde qualiter fitia regis omnibus alijs retictis appollinum maritu 〈…〉 preclegit bylles wel receyued ſhe hath al hir loues weyued thouȝt yt thā tyme ſpace put hir faders grace wrote ageyn thus ſhe ſayd ſhame mayde ſpeche dare • vnloke wryfyng may ſpoke wryte fader thus yf haue apollynus al world ſo beſyde wyl none man abyde certes yf hym fayle wote right wel without fayle ye ſhal faderles lettre came preſe tofore kyng ſtode whan vnderſtode yaue hem auſwer pryuelye ••• e • f counceyl wyſte toke leue hem lyſte wente forth vpon theyr weys kyng wold bewreye counceyl maner hye ſuffreth tyl tyme ſye qualiter rex regina maritagium filie ſue cum appolino conſencierunt whan chambre come counceyl therto hym nome man tyre lete hym ſee lettre al pryuyte doughter hym ſente knee grounde bente thonked hym hyr alſo wente thenne two good herte good corage ful loue ful mariage kyng hole accorded whan recorded vnto doughter ſtode yefte al worldes good ne ſhold haue made hir halfe ſo blythe forth al kyng aſſwithe wyl haue hir good aſſent hath quene hir moder ſente quene comen ſhe herde matere ferde ſawe debate ſhe ſawe dyſeſe yf ſhe wold hir doughter pleſe therto aſſented ful dede wonderful man knewe ſoth •• hym ſelf man netheleſſe ſo hym thought dedes ſothe wrought come gentyl blood hym lacketh worldes good therof dyſpeyre ſhe ſhal hir faderes heyre able gouerne thus wyl loue werne hym hyr wyſe al accorded deuyſe qualiter appollinus filie regies nup • ſit et primo nocte cum ea concubiens ipſam inpregnauit day tyme mariage loue lorde corage hym thynketh longe ſpede atte laſte vnto dede tyme come wyſe grete offryng ſacrefyſe wedde make grete feſte euery thynge right neſte within hows eke without ſo done al aboute grete worſhyp grete nobleſſe cryed many man largeſſe vnto lordes hygh loude knyghtes yonge prowde iuſte fyrſt daunce day goo nyghtes chaunce hath derked al bright ſonne lord hath loue wonne goo bed wyf lede luſty lyf ſomdele ſene pleyden hem bytwene gete chylde betwene hem two fyl mochel woo qualiter amtaſſiatores tiro quodam naui pentapolim veniētes mortem regis antiochi appollino nūciauerūt haue tolde ſpouſayles ſpeke meruayles afterward hem byfelle • wonder telle fyl day rode kyng quene al route pleye hem vpon ſeconde ſeen toward londe ſhyp ſaylyng grete araye knowe mene may tyl come abyde ſawe ſtonde euery ſyde endlong ſhyppes borde ſhewe penonnes ryche rewe ax • whan ſhyp come fro tyre anone anſwerd ſomme ouer ſayden cauſe comen fore ſeche fynde appollynus kynde hir lyege lord appereth tale hereth riȝt glad hym tolde vengeaunce god wolde antyochus men may wyte fire lyghtenyng al ſmyte doughter hath ſame chaunce ben bothe one balaunce thy lyege lord ſeye name al londe preye lefte al thynge done lyke come ſone ſee owne lyege men ben ken lyuen longyng deſyre tyl ye come ageyn tyre tole kyng pentapolyn al ouer ſprad ioye ſeche euery man ſpeche ſayden al one acoorde worthy kyng ſhal ben lorde thouȝt v firſt heuyneſſe ſhape v grete gladneſſe qualiter appollino cum vxore ſua imprignata pentapoli verſus tyrum nauigantiꝰ contigit vxorem mortis artia •• anguſtiatam naui filiam que poſtea thayſies vocabatur patere tthus goeth tydyng ouer al nede muſt nede ſhal appollynus leue took god al bonde bytook al peple longe brode lenger abode kyng quene ſorow made yet ſomdele glade ſuche thynge herde tho thus bytwene wele woo ſhyp goeth wyf childe euer meke mylde wold departe hym fro suche loue bytwene hem two lycho rida hir offyce take norice wende yonge wyf ſhape wooful lyf within tyme betyd ſee amyd northe ſee cloude ſtorme awos wyndes loud blewen many dredeſul blaſte welken al ouer caſte derke nyght ſonne hath vnder ther grete tempeſt thondre mone eke ſterres bothe blacke clowdes hem clothe wherof bright loke hyde yonge lady wepte cryde comforte myght auayle chylde ſhe began trauayle ſhe laye caban choos wooful lord fro hir awos longe ony morowe anguyſſhe ſorowe delyuerd al nyght dede euery mannes ſyght netheleſſe al woo mayde chylde boren tho qualiter appollinus mortem vxoris ſue planxit appollynus thys kuewe ſwowne hym ſelf ouerthrewe man wyſt hym lyf woke ſaid wyf ioye luſt deſyre welth recoueryre ſhal lyue thou ſhalt dye ha thou fortune defye haſt thou thy werſte herte ne wyl thou breſte forth hir myght paſſe paynes moche laſſe ſuche wepyng ſuche crye dede wyf laye hym bye thouſand ſythes hir kyſte neuer man ſawe ne wyſte ſorowe ſorowe lyche euer emonge vpon lyche fyl ſwownyng thouȝt owne deth beſought vnto goddes al aboue many pytous worde loue ſuche wordes tho herde neuer mannes eere onely thylke ſayed mayſter ſhypman came prayed ſuche ben therin ſayn may thyng wyn ageyn deth hym rede wel ware take hede ſee weye nature receyue may creature within hym ſelf holde dede thy wolde counceyllen al aboute deed body caſten oute better ſayden alle hir ſo byfalle yf ſholden al ſpylle kyng vnderſtode wylle knewe counceyl trewe began ageyn ſorowe newe pytous herte thus ſeye al reſon ye preye qualiter ſuadentibu • nautis corpus vxoris ſue mortue quadam ciſta plumbo et ferro obtuſa circumligata tempus inſtat ſcundum aliquid allemare cupiens inter labores et ocia ad aliorum noti • iam tres libros doctrine cauſa forma ſubſequenti propterea compoſuit primus liber galico ſermone editus decem diuiditur partes tractans de viais et virtutibus necnon de bariis huius ſeculi gradibus nama que qui peccator trauſgreſſus ad ſui creatoris agnicionem redire debet recto tramite docere conatur titulus libelli iſtius speculū hominis nuncupatus eſt scandus enim liber ſermone latino verſibus exame tri compoſitus tractat ſuper illo mirabi • euentu qui anglia tempore regis ricardi ſecundi anno regni ſui quarto contigit quando ſeruiles ruſtici impetuoſe contra nobiles et ingenuos regni inſurrexerūt innocenciam tamen dicti domini regis tune iunioris etatis cauſam inde excuſabilem pronuncians
